<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1257001546" /><table class="infobox vevent"><caption class="infobox-title summary">Google Cloud App</caption><tbody><tr style="display: none;"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1257001546" /></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header"><a href="/wiki/Software_release_life_cycle" title="Software release life cycle">Stable release(s)</a> <span class="plainlinks" style="font-size:smaller; margin:0px"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Template:Latest_stable_software_release/Google_Cloud_App?action=edit">&#91;±&#93;</a></span></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1257001546" /><table class="infobox-subbox"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Android</th><td class="infobox-data">1.24 (Build 731635878) / 27&#160;February 2025<span class="noprint">&#59;&#32;19 days ago</span><span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2025-02-27</span>)</span><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">iOS</th><td class="infobox-data">1.28.462 / 1&#160;March 2025<span class="noprint">&#59;&#32;17 days ago</span><span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2025-03-01</span>)</span><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Computing_platform" title="Computing platform">Platform</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>, <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://cloud.google.com/">cloud<wbr />.google<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Google Cloud Platform</b> (<b>GCP</b>) is a suite of <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a> services offered by <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> that provides a series of modular cloud services including computing, <a href="/wiki/Computer_data_storage" title="Computer data storage">data storage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Data_analysis" title="Data analysis">data analytics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Machine_learning" title="Machine learning">machine learning</a>, alongside a set of management tools.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It runs on the same infrastructure that Google uses internally for its end-user products, such as <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google Search</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gmail" title="Gmail">Gmail</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Google_Docs" title="Google Docs">Google Docs</a>, according to Verma et al.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Registration requires a credit card or bank account details.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Google Cloud Platform provides <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure_as_a_service" title="Infrastructure as a service">infrastructure as a service</a>, <a href="/wiki/Platform_as_a_service" title="Platform as a service">platform as a service</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Serverless_computing" title="Serverless computing">serverless computing</a> environments.
</p><p>In April 2008, Google announced <a href="/wiki/Google_App_Engine" title="Google App Engine">App Engine</a>, a platform for developing and hosting web applications in Google-managed <a href="/wiki/Data_center" title="Data center">data centers</a>, which was the first cloud computing service from the company. The service became generally available in November 2011. Since the announcement of App Engine, Google added multiple cloud services to the platform.
</p><p>Google Cloud Platform is a part<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> of <b>Google Cloud</b>, which includes the Google Cloud Platform public cloud infrastructure, as well as <a href="/wiki/Google_Workspace" title="Google Workspace">Google Workspace</a> (G Suite), enterprise versions of <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> and <a href="/wiki/ChromeOS" title="ChromeOS">ChromeOS</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" class="mw-redirect" title="Application programming interface">application programming interfaces</a> (APIs) for machine learning and enterprise mapping services. Since at least 2022,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Google's official materials have stated that "Google Cloud" is the new name for "Google Cloud Platform," which may cause naming confusion.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Challenges">Challenges</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Challenges"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Like other <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a> solutions, applications hosted on <b>Google Cloud Platform</b> are subject to the <a href="/wiki/Fallacies_of_distributed_computing" title="Fallacies of distributed computing">fallacies of distributed computing</a>, a series of misconceptions that can lead to significant issues in software development and deployment. <sup id="cite_ref-:02_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Products">Products</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Products"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Kubernetes_talk_at_Google_Cloud_Summit.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Kubernetes_talk_at_Google_Cloud_Summit.jpg/220px-Kubernetes_talk_at_Google_Cloud_Summit.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Kubernetes_talk_at_Google_Cloud_Summit.jpg/330px-Kubernetes_talk_at_Google_Cloud_Summit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Kubernetes_talk_at_Google_Cloud_Summit.jpg/440px-Kubernetes_talk_at_Google_Cloud_Summit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a><figcaption>Conference presentation on Google Container Engine/Kubernetes</figcaption></figure><p>Google lists over 100 products under the Google Cloud brand. Some of the key services are listed below.
</p><div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Compute">Compute</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Compute"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Google_App_Engine" title="Google App Engine">App Engine</a> – <a href="/wiki/Platform_as_a_service" title="Platform as a service">Platform as a Service</a> to deploy applications developed with <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Node.js" title="Node.js">Node.js</a>, <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a>, <a href="/wiki/C_Sharp_(programming_language)" title="C Sharp (programming language)">C#</a>, <a href="/wiki/.NET_Framework" title=".NET Framework">.Net</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruby_(programming_language)" title="Ruby (programming language)">Ruby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Go_(programming_language)" title="Go (programming language)">Go</a> programming languages.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Google_Compute_Engine" title="Google Compute Engine">Compute Engine</a> – <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure_as_a_service" title="Infrastructure as a service">Infrastructure as a Service</a> to run <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> virtual machines.</li>
<li>Google Kubernetes Engine (GKE) or GKE <a href="/wiki/On-premises_software" title="On-premises software">on-prem</a> offered as part of Anthos platform<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> – Containers as a Service based on <a href="/wiki/Kubernetes" title="Kubernetes">Kubernetes</a>.</li>
<li>Cloud Functions – <a href="/wiki/Function_as_a_service" title="Function as a service">Functions as a Service</a> to run event-driven code written in Node.js, Java, Python, or Go.</li>
<li>Cloud Run – Compute execution environment based on Knative.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Offered as Cloud Run (fully managed)<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or as Cloud Run for Anthos.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Currently supports GCP, AWS and VMware management.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Storage_and_databases">Storage and databases</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Storage and databases"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Google_Cloud_Storage" title="Google Cloud Storage">Cloud Storage</a> – <a href="/wiki/Object_storage" title="Object storage">Object storage</a> with integrated edge caching to store <a href="/wiki/Unstructured_data" title="Unstructured data">unstructured data</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_SQL&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Google Cloud SQL (page does not exist)">Cloud SQL</a> – <a href="/wiki/Cloud_database" title="Cloud database">Database as a Service</a> based on <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a>, <a href="/wiki/PostgreSQL" title="PostgreSQL">PostgreSQL</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_SQL_Server" title="Microsoft SQL Server">Microsoft SQL Server</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bigtable" title="Bigtable">Cloud Bigtable</a> – Managed <a href="/wiki/NoSQL" title="NoSQL">NoSQL</a> database service.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spanner_(database)" title="Spanner (database)">Cloud Spanner</a> – Horizontally scalable, strongly consistent, <a href="/wiki/Relational_database_management_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Relational database management system">relational database service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Google_Cloud_Datastore" title="Google Cloud Datastore">Cloud Datastore</a> – NoSQL database for web and mobile applications.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Persistent Disk – <a href="/wiki/Block_(data_storage)" title="Block (data storage)">Block storage</a> for Compute Engine virtual machines.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Memorystore – Managed in-memory data store based on <a href="/wiki/Redis" title="Redis">Redis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Memcached" title="Memcached">Memcached</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Local <a href="/wiki/Solid-state_drive" title="Solid-state drive">SSD</a>: High-performance, transient, local block storage.</li>
<li>Filestore: High-performance file storage for Google Cloud users.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>AlloyDB: Fully managed PostgreSQL database service.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Networking">Networking</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Networking"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Google_Cloud_Network_Topology_-_External_Load_Balancer_Architecture.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Google_Cloud_Network_Topology_-_External_Load_Balancer_Architecture.png/242px-Google_Cloud_Network_Topology_-_External_Load_Balancer_Architecture.png" decoding="async" width="242" height="104" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Google_Cloud_Network_Topology_-_External_Load_Balancer_Architecture.png/363px-Google_Cloud_Network_Topology_-_External_Load_Balancer_Architecture.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Google_Cloud_Network_Topology_-_External_Load_Balancer_Architecture.png/484px-Google_Cloud_Network_Topology_-_External_Load_Balancer_Architecture.png 2x" data-file-width="1366" data-file-height="589" /></a><figcaption></figcaption></figure>
<ul><li>VPC – <a href="/wiki/Virtual_private_cloud" title="Virtual private cloud">Virtual Private Cloud</a> for managing the <a href="/wiki/Software-defined_networking" title="Software-defined networking">software defined network</a> of cloud resources.</li></ul>
<ul><li>Cloud Load Balancing – Software-defined, managed service for <a href="/wiki/Cloud_load_balancing" title="Cloud load balancing">load balancing</a> the traffic.</li>
<li>Cloud Armor – <a href="/wiki/Web_application_firewall" title="Web application firewall">Web application firewall</a> to protect workloads from <a href="/wiki/Denial-of-service_attack" title="Denial-of-service attack">DDoS</a> attacks.</li>
<li>Cloud CDN – <a href="/wiki/Content_delivery_network" title="Content delivery network">Content Delivery Network</a> based on Google's globally distributed edge points of presence.</li>
<li>Cloud Interconnect – Service to connect a data center with Google Cloud Platform</li>
<li>Cloud DNS – Managed, authoritative <a href="/wiki/DNS_hosting" class="mw-redirect" title="DNS hosting">DNS hosting</a> service running on the same infrastructure as Google.</li>
<li>Network Service Tiers – Option to choose Premium vs Standard network tier for higher-performing network.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Big_data">Big data</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Big data"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/BigQuery" title="BigQuery">BigQuery</a> – Scalable, managed enterprise <a href="/wiki/Data_warehouse" title="Data warehouse">data warehouse</a> for analytics.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Google_Cloud_Dataflow" title="Google Cloud Dataflow">Cloud Dataflow</a> – Managed service based on <a href="/wiki/Apache_Beam" title="Apache Beam">Apache Beam</a> for stream and batch data processing.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Data Fusion – A managed <a href="/wiki/Extract,_transform,_load" title="Extract, transform, load">ETL</a> service based on the Open Source Cask Data Application Platform.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Dataproc – <a href="/wiki/Big_data" title="Big data">Big data</a> platform for running <a href="/wiki/Apache_Hadoop" title="Apache Hadoop">Apache Hadoop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Apache_Spark" title="Apache Spark">Apache Spark</a> jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Composer – Managed workflow orchestration service built on <a href="/wiki/Apache_Airflow" title="Apache Airflow">Apache Airflow</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Datalab – Tool for <a href="/wiki/Data_exploration" title="Data exploration">data exploration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Analysis" title="Analysis">analysis</a>, visualization and machine learning. This is a fully managed Jupyter Notebook service.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Dataprep – Data service based on <a href="/wiki/Trifacta" title="Trifacta">Trifacta</a> to visually explore, clean, and prepare data for analysis.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Pub/Sub – Scalable event ingestion service based on <a href="/wiki/Message_queue" title="Message queue">message queues</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Looker_Studio" title="Looker Studio">Looker Studio</a> – <a href="/wiki/Business_intelligence" title="Business intelligence">Business intelligence</a> tool to visualize data through dashboards and reports.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Looker_(company)" title="Looker (company)">Looker</a> – Business intelligence platform.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cloud_AI">Cloud AI</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Cloud AI"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Cloud AutoML – Service to train and deploy custom machine learning models. As of September 2018, the service is in Beta.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud <a href="/wiki/Tensor_processing_unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Tensor processing unit">TPU</a> – Accelerators used by Google to train machine learning models.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Machine Learning Engine – Managed service for training and building machine learning models based on mainstream frameworks.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Talent Solution (formerly Cloud Job Discovery) – Service based on Google's search and machine learning capabilities for the recruiting ecosystem.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Dialogflow Enterprise – Development environment based on Google's machine learning for building <a href="/wiki/Natural-language_user_interface" title="Natural-language user interface">conversational interfaces</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Natural Language – Text analysis service based on Google <a href="/wiki/Deep_learning" title="Deep learning">Deep Learning</a> models.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Speech-to-Text – <a href="/wiki/Speech_recognition" title="Speech recognition">Speech to text</a> conversion service based on machine learning.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Text-to-Speech – <a href="/wiki/Speech_synthesis" title="Speech synthesis">Text to speech</a> conversion service based on machine learning.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Translation API – Service to dynamically translate between thousands of available language pairs.</li>
<li>Cloud Vision API – <a href="/wiki/Image_analysis" title="Image analysis">Image analysis</a> service based on machine learning.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Video Intelligence – <a href="/wiki/Video_content_analysis" title="Video content analysis">Video analysis</a> service based on machine learning.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Management_tools">Management tools</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Management tools"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Operations suite (formerly <a href="/wiki/Stackdriver" title="Stackdriver">Stackdriver</a> ) – Monitoring, logging, tracing, and diagnostics for applications on Google Cloud Platform.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Deployment Manager &#160;- Tool to deploy Google Cloud Platform resources defined in templates created in <a href="/wiki/YAML" title="YAML">YAML</a>, <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a> or <a href="/wiki/Jinja_(template_engine)" title="Jinja (template engine)">Jinja2</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Cloud Console – Web interface to manage Google Cloud Platform resources.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Google_cloud_shell" class="mw-redirect" title="Google cloud shell">Cloud Shell</a> – Browser-based shell command-line access to manage Google Cloud Platform resources.</li>
<li>Cloud Console Mobile App – <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> and <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> application to manage Google Cloud Platform resources.</li>
<li>Cloud APIs – <a href="/wiki/API" title="API">APIs</a> to programmatically access Google Cloud Platform resources</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Identity_and_security">Identity and security</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Identity and security"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Cloud Identity – <a href="/wiki/Single_sign-on" title="Single sign-on">Single sign-on</a> (SSO) service based on <a href="/wiki/SAML_2.0" title="SAML 2.0">SAML 2.0</a> and <a href="/wiki/OpenID" title="OpenID">OpenID</a>.</li>
<li>Cloud IAM – <a href="/wiki/Identity_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Identity management">Identity &amp; Access Management</a> (IAM) service for defining policies based on <a href="/wiki/Role-based_access_control" title="Role-based access control">role-based access control</a>.</li>
<li>Cloud Identity-Aware Proxy – Service to control access to cloud applications running on Google Cloud Platform without using a <a href="/wiki/Virtual_private_network" title="Virtual private network">VPN</a>.</li>
<li>Cloud Data Loss Prevention API – Service to automatically discover, classify, and redact sensitive data.</li>
<li>Security Key Enforcement – <a href="/wiki/Multi-factor_authentication" title="Multi-factor authentication">Two-step verification</a> service based on a security key.</li>
<li>Cloud Key Management Service – Cloud-hosted key management service integrated with IAM and audit logging.</li>
<li>Cloud Resource Manager – Service to manage resources by project, folder, and organization based on the hierarchy.</li>
<li>Cloud Security Command Center – Security and data risk platform for data and services running in Google Cloud Platform.</li>
<li>Cloud Security Scanner – Automated <a href="/wiki/Vulnerability_(computing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vulnerability (computing)">vulnerability scanning</a> service for applications deployed in App Engine.</li>
<li>Access Transparency – Near real-time audit logs providing visibility to Google Cloud Platform administrators.</li>
<li>VPC Service Controls – Service to manage security perimeters for sensitive data in Google Cloud Platform services.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Internet_of_things_(IoT)"><span id="Internet_of_things_.28IoT.29"></span>Internet of things (IoT)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Internet of things (IoT)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Cloud IoT Core – Secure device connection and management service for <a href="/wiki/Internet_of_things" title="Internet of things">Internet of Things</a>.</li>
<li>Edge TPU – Purpose-built ASIC designed to run inference at the edge. As of September 2018, this product is in private beta.</li>
<li>Cloud IoT Edge – Brings AI to the <a href="/wiki/Edge_computing" title="Edge computing">edge computing</a> layer.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="API_platform">API platform</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: API platform"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Maps Platform – APIs for maps, routes, and places based on Google Maps.</li>
<li>Apigee API Platform – Lifecycle management platform to design, secure, deploy, monitor, and scale APIs.</li>
<li>API Monetization – Tool for API providers to create revenue models, reports, <a href="/wiki/Payment_gateway" title="Payment gateway">payment gateways</a>, and developer portal integrations.</li>
<li>Developer Portal – Self-service platform for developers to publish and manage APIs.</li>
<li>API Analytics – Service to analyze API-driven programs through monitoring, measuring, and managing APIs.</li>
<li>Apigee Sense – Enables API security by identifying and alerting administrators to suspicious API behaviors.</li>
<li>Cloud Endpoints – An <a href="/wiki/Nginx" title="Nginx">NGINX</a>-based proxy to deploy and manage APIs.</li>
<li>Service Infrastructure – A set of foundational services for building Google Cloud products.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Regions_and_zones">Regions and zones</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Regions and zones"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A region is a specific geographical location where users can deploy cloud resources. Each region is an independent geographic area that consists of zones.
</p><p>A zone is a deployment area for Google Cloud Platform resources within a region. Zones should be considered a single failure domain within a region. Most regions have three zones. 
</p><p>As of Q1 2024<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Google Cloud Platform is available in 40 regions and 121 zones. This is a list of those regions and zones:<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Similarity_to_services_by_other_cloud_service_providers">Similarity to services by other cloud service providers</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Similarity to services by other cloud service providers"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cloud-computing_comparison" title="Cloud-computing comparison">Cloud-computing comparison</a></div>
<p>For those familiar with other notable cloud service providers, a comparison of similar services may be helpful in understanding Google Cloud Platform's offerings.
</p>

</th>

</th></tr>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Timeline">Timeline</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Timeline"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:GoogleCloudSummitKeynote.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/GoogleCloudSummitKeynote.jpg/220px-GoogleCloudSummitKeynote.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/GoogleCloudSummitKeynote.jpg/330px-GoogleCloudSummitKeynote.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/GoogleCloudSummitKeynote.jpg/440px-GoogleCloudSummitKeynote.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a><figcaption>Google Cloud Summit in 2017</figcaption></figure>
<ul><li><b>April 2008</b> – Google App Engine announced in preview<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>May 2010</b> – Google Cloud Storage launched<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>May 2010</b> – Google BigQuery and Prediction API announced in preview<sup id="cite_ref-auto3_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>October 2011</b> – Google Cloud SQL is announced in preview<sup id="cite_ref-auto3_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>June 2012</b> – Google Compute Engine is launched in preview<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>May 2013</b> – Google Compute Engine is released to GA<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>August 2013</b> -  Cloud Storage begins automatically encrypting each Storage object's data and <a href="/wiki/Metadata" title="Metadata">metadata</a> under the 128-bit <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Encryption_Standard" title="Advanced Encryption Standard">Advanced Encryption Standard</a> (AES-128), and each encryption key is itself encrypted with a regularly rotated set of master keys<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>February 2014</b> – Google Cloud SQL becomes GA<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>May 2014</b> – Stackdriver is acquired by Google<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>June 2014</b> – Kubernetes is announced as an open source container manager<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>June 2014</b> – Cloud Dataflow is announced in preview<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>October 2014</b> – Google acquires Firebase<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>November 2014</b> – Alpha release Google Kubernetes Engine (formerly Container Engine) is announced<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>January 2015</b> – Google Cloud Monitoring based on Stackdriver goes into Beta<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>March 2015</b> – Google Cloud Pub/Sub becomes available in Beta<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>April 2015</b> – Google Cloud DNS becomes generally available<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>April 2015</b> – Google Dataflow launched in beta<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>July 2015</b> – Google releases v1 of Kubernetes; Hands it over to The Cloud Native Computing Foundation</li>
<li><b>August 2015</b> – Google Cloud Dataflow, Google Cloud Pub/Sub, Google Kubernetes Engine, and Deployment Manager graduate to GA<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>November 2015</b> – Bebop is acquired, and Diane Greene joins Google<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>February 2016</b> – Google Cloud Functions becomes available in Alpha<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>September 2016</b> – Apigee, a provider of application programming interface (API) management company, is acquired by Google<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>September 2016</b> – Stackdriver becomes generally available<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>November 2016</b> – Qwiklabs, an EdTech company is acquired by Google<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>February 2017</b> – Cloud Spanner, highly available, globally-distributed database is released into Beta<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>March 2017</b> – Google acquires Kaggle, world's largest community of data scientists and machine learning enthusiasts<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>April 2017</b> – MIT professor <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Sutherland_(mathematician)" title="Andrew Sutherland (mathematician)">Andrew Sutherland</a> breaks the record for the largest ever Compute Engine cluster with 220,000 cores on Preemptible VMs.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>May 2017</b> – Google Cloud IoT Core is launched in Beta<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>November 2017</b> – Google Kubernetes Engine gets certified by the CNCF<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>February 2018</b> – Google Cloud IoT Core becomes generally available<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>February 2018</b> – Google announces its intent to acquire Xively<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>February 2018</b> – Cloud TPUs, ML accelerators for Tensorflow, become available in Beta<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>May 2018</b> – Google Cloud Memorystore becomes available in Beta<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>April 2019</b> – Google Cloud Run (fully managed) Beta release<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>April 2019</b> – Google Anthos announced<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>November 2019</b> – Google Cloud Run (fully managed) General availability release<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>March 2020</b> – Due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, Google Cloud postponed the online streaming version of its Google Cloud Next mega-conference, two weeks after it canceled the in-person version.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>October 2020</b> – Google Cloud announced that it will become a block producer candidate for the EOS network and <a href="/wiki/EOS.IO" title="EOS.IO">EOS.IO</a> protocol. Currently the top block producers are <a href="/wiki/Cryptocurrency" title="Cryptocurrency">cryptocurrency</a> exchanges like <a href="/wiki/OKEx" class="mw-redirect" title="OKEx">OKEx</a> and Binance.<sup id="cite_ref-Google_Cloud_2020-10-09_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Google_Cloud_2020-10-09-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_2020-10-09_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_2020-10-09-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>February 2021</b> – Google Kubernetes Engine Autopilot introduced. <sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>May 2021</b> – Vertex AI announced at Google.io <sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>June 2021</b> – In 2021, Apple was Google Cloud's biggest customer.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>April 2022</b> – MobiledgeX acquired and joins Google Cloud.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>March 2023</b> – Google brings <a href="/wiki/Generative_AI" class="mw-redirect" title="Generative AI">generative AI</a> capabilities to Google Cloud.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>May 2024</b> Google Cloud partnered with <a href="/wiki/Airtel" class="mw-redirect" title="Airtel">Airtel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Public_Customers">Public Customers</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Cloud_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Public Customers"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Customers announced in 2023 include: <a href="/wiki/Kingfisher_plc" title="Kingfisher plc">Kingfisher plc</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Kuwait" title="Government of Kuwait">Government of Kuwait</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_B%C3%B6rse_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Deutsche Börse Group">Deutsche Börse Group</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Unity_Technologies" title="Unity Technologies">Unity Technologies</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Uber" title="Uber">Uber</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/FanCode" title="FanCode">FanCode</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Daimler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
